# Analysis of Ground Truth

The GT expression is:
$$f(x,t) = -1.15357x - 1.15357x\exp(-|x|) + 0.42262\sin(t)$$

This can be rewritten as:
$$f(x,t) = -1.15357x(1 + \exp(-|x|)) + 0.42262\sin(t)$$

Key structural features:
1. A term linear in $x$: $-1.15357x$
2. A term $x\exp(-|x|)$: $-1.15357x\exp(-|x|)$
3. A sinusoidal term in $t$: $0.42262\sin(t)$

The critical feature is the $x\exp(-|x|)$ term, which involves both $x$ and $|x|$ (absolute value). This is a very specific nonlinear function of $x$ alone.

# Candidate Analysis

Let me check each candidate for the presence of the required basis functions.

**Required basis functions:** $x$, $x\exp(-|x|)$, $\sin(t)$

The key question is: does any candidate contain a term that can represent $x\exp(-|x|)$?

Let me scan through the candidates:

- **Candidates 1-5, 49-50**: Contain $x^3$, $x^2$, $\exp(t)$, $x/(c+t)^5$ terms. None have $\exp(-|x|)$ or $x\exp(-|x|)$. Polynomials in $x$ cannot represent $x\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidates 6**: Two sine terms in $t$, linear in $x$. Missing $x\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidates 7, 16, 18, 19**: Contain $\log(cx+1)$. This is not equivalent to $x\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 8**: Has $\exp(c_5 x)$, but the term is $c_4\exp(c_5 x)$, not $x\exp(-|x|)$. These are different functions. **No match.**

- **Candidates 9-10**: Have $x/(c+t)^5$. Not equivalent to $x\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidates 11-14**: Rational functions of $t$ and $x$. None contain $\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 15**: Has $c_5\exp(c_6 x)$. This is $\exp(cx)$, not $x\exp(-|x|)$. For $x > 0$, we'd need $x\exp(-x)$, but $\exp(cx)$ alone (without the $x$ multiplier) cannot match $x\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 17**: Has $c_4 x(c_5+t)^{c_6}$. This is a power of $t$ times $x$, not $x\exp(-|x|)$. **No match.**

- **Candidates 20-48**: These are combinations of $x$, $\sin(t)$, rational functions of $t$, and constants. None contain $\exp(-|x|)$ or any exponential in $x$. **No match.**

None of the candidates contain the essential $x\exp(-|x|)$ term. Since $x\exp(-|x|)$ is linearly independent from all the basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials in $x$, $\exp(x)$, $\log(x)$, rational functions of $t$, $\sin(t)$, power functions of $t$), no candidate can be algebraically equivalent to the GT.

The absolute value in $\exp(-|x|)$ makes this even more restrictive - none of the candidates even have an absolute value operation.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-1.15357191344644*x - 1.15357191344644*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.422619160916855*sin(t)`

The GT has three terms:
1. A linear term in x: `c_a * x`
2. A term `c_b * x * exp(-|x|)`: This is a product of x with an exponential of |x|
3. A sinusoidal term in t: `c_c * sin(t)`

The key challenge is the `x*exp(-|x|)` term. This is NOT equivalent to any polynomial, rational function, logarithmic function, or simple exponential in x or t. Let me check each candidate for the presence of this basis function.

**Key observations:**
- `x*exp(-|x|)` is a specific nonlinear function of x that cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, logarithms, or exponentials of t.
- No candidate contains `exp(-Abs(x))` or `exp(-|x|)` or anything that could produce `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Let me scan through all candidates:

- **Candidates 1-5, 49-50**: Contain polynomials in x (x², x³), exp(t), and power terms like x/(c+t)^5. None have exp(-|x|).
- **Candidate 6**: Two sin terms. No x*exp(-|x|).
- **Candidates 7, 16, 18-19**: Contain log(c*x+1). log is not exp(-|x|).
- **Candidate 8, 15**: Contains exp(c*x). Setting c5=0 eliminates it, but then we lose the x*exp(-|x|) term entirely.
- **Candidates 9-10**: x/(c+t)^5 terms. Not exp(-|x|).
- **Candidates 11-14**: Rational functions of t and x. Cannot produce x*exp(-|x|).
- **Candidate 17**: x*(c5+t)^c6 - a power law in t, not exp(-|x|).
- **Candidates 20-48**: Various combinations of linear x, sin(t), rational functions of t, log(t), t^c, etc. None contain exp(-|x|) or exp(x) terms that could match.

For **Candidate 8**: `c0*x + c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c4*exp(c5*x) + c6*t/(c7*t + c8) + c9/(c7*t + c8)`
- This has exp(c5*x), not exp(-|x|). For x > 0, exp(c5*x) with c5 < 0 gives exp(-x), but for x < 0, exp(c5*x) gives exp(-(-x)) = exp(x) ≠ exp(-|x|) = exp(-(-x)) = exp(x). Wait - actually for x < 0, |x| = -x, so exp(-|x|) = exp(x). And exp(c5*x) with c5 = 1 gives exp(x). So for x < 0, they'd match. But for x > 0, exp(-|x|) = exp(-x) and exp(c5*x) = exp(x) with c5=1. These can't match simultaneously. exp(c5*x) is smooth and monotonic; exp(-|x|) has a kink at 0. They cannot be equal.

**Candidate 15**: `c0*x + c1 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*exp(c6*x) + c7*x`
Same issue - exp(c6*x) cannot match x*exp(-|x|).

None of the candidates contain the essential `x*exp(-|x|)` basis function, which is linearly independent from all basis functions present in the candidates.
